<system_prompt>
MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: VFX & COMPUTE PARTICLES
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Optimize particle compute shader"
OPERATIONAL MODE: GPU DOMINANCE / FILL-RATE OPTIMIZATION
CONSTRAINTS: COMPUTE SHADERS ONLY, 0 CPU ALLOCATIONS, STAGGERED SAMPLING, ALPHATOMASK.

[0. SITREP: THE INVISIBLE OVERHEAD]
You were updating 100,000 particles every frame without Frustum Culling and pushing compute parameters (SetVector/SetFloat) every tick regardless of state changes. This is wasteful. You will implement dirty-checking for bindings, move far-field culling to a staggered cadence, and brutally optimize the fill-rate.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE & BORDER CONTROL]
1. Open Hecton_MarineSnow.compute and HectonMarineSnowRenderer.cs.
2. Identify where length(), distance(), or sqrt() is used for collision or falloff. Delete them.
3. Locate every SetBuffer, SetFloat, and SetVector in the Update loop.
4. You do not touch the Ocean Kinematics. You read the Flow Field data provided by the Fluid Engineer.

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE GPU STORM (25 TASKS)]

-- COMPUTE SHADER CHEATS (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. STAGGERED ABYSSAL FLOW SAMPLING: Do not sample the 3D flow field for every particle every frame. Use a bitmask-based stagger: only 25% of particles sample the flow field per frame based on ((particleIndex + frame) & 3) == 0.
2. SDF BUBBLE COLLISION (1-TAP FAKE): Replace the 7-tap SDF gradient bounce with a 1-tap SDF sample. If density < 0, reflect velocity by a precomputed "Ceiling Slap" normal and add random horizontal jitter.
3. PROP-WASH SQUARED FALLOFF: Calculate thruster influence using squared distance: if (distSq < thrusterRadiusSq). Use cheap dominant-axis direction instead of math.normalize().
4. 10HZ COLD BINDING REFRESH: Non-vector compute parameters (SDF textures, terrain metadata) must move to a 0.1s ColdTick refresh. Only per-frame vectors (camera pos) are allowed in the hot Update push.
5. WHALE PULSE SHOCKWAVE: Single expanding sphere mesh with a refractive shader sampling SceneColor and SceneDepth. No extra camera passes. No particle spam for shockwaves.

-- FILL-RATE & RENDERING --
6. ALPHATOMASK DITHERED CUTOUT: Remove clip()/discard from particle shaders. Switch to AlphaToMask On with Dithered Cutout for more efficient hardware anti-aliasing.
7. HALF-RES PARTICLE COMPOSITING: Render transparent particles into a Half-Resolution off-screen buffer. Composite using 1 particle sample + 1 depth sample + raw-depth derivative edge fade (no 5-tap bilateral upsample).
8. COMPUTE FRUSTUM CULLING (INDIRECT): Use Camera's View-Projection matrix. If a particle is outside the frustum, do not append it to the AppendStructuredBuffer.
9. VOLUMETRIC FOG INJECTION: Compute particles write to a low-res density buffer that the Volumetric Fog pass samples. Use a 25% staggered atomic addition.
10. SONAR GLOW SPLAT: Replace 9-tap splat per particle with 1-tap, 25% staggered atomic accumulation.

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY & HYGIENE --
11. DIRTY-CHECKED GLOBALS: Flora biolum color/strength and Half-Res Active toggles must ONLY publish to Shader.SetGlobalFloat when changed. Remove redundant per-frame pushes.
12. LASER CUTTING SPARK MAP: Use simple gravity * time falloff combined with fixed 8-way direction LUT for sparks. Replace Quaternion.LookRotation with dominant-axis precomputed quaternions.
13. BIOLUMINESCENCE WAVE SYNC: Sync coral emission pulses through _GlobalBiolumPhase. Use math.frac and a triangle wave for the pulse, not a Sine wave.
14. STRUCT ALIGNMENT: Ensure Marine Snow particle is padded to exactly 64B, and frame constants to 112B (16B aligned), with explicit sequential layout.
15. MEMORY BOUNDARY PROTECTION: Implement a hard cap of 32,768 particles for MX350 profiles. If the system requests more, simply ignore the spawn request.

[III. MICRO-OPTIMIZATIONS (10 TASKS)]
16. Replace math.sin laser jitter with triangle-wave frac/abs in LaserCutter.cs.
17. Replace clip-space division in particles with rcp(w) multiply.
18. Replace float divisions for dispatch group sizing with bit shifts (e.g., (count + 63) >> 6).
19. Cache fog-density dispatch groups and texel reciprocals at resize time.
20. Fix any Archivarius naming violations in LaserCutter.cs or HectonMarineSnowRenderer.cs (e.g., mojibake/Cyrillic in comments).
21. Precalculate RadiusSq and InvRadiusSq (reciprocal) for Cavitation Burst Events upon enqueue.
22. Replace epsilon math.abs dirty check for binary flags with exact 0/1 compare.
23. Ensure _MarineSnowPropwashParams is moved to the cold binding refresh.
24. Verify AlphaToMask is correctly setup in the pass block of the shader.
25. Remove any duplicate [StructLayout] attributes blocking the Core compile.

[IV. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]
1. Show the Compute Shader code for the 1-tap SDF Bubble Collision.
2. Show the ShouldRunQuarterRate bitmask helper implementation.
3. List the parameters successfully moved to the 10Hz ColdTick refresh.
4. STATUS: MUST BE "PENDING VERIFICATION".

What Was Wrong
Marine snow flow/SDF/propwash paths were carrying unnecessary hot work: full-rate abyssal flow sampling risk, expensive SDF collision pattern, propwash direction/falloff cost, and cold external bindings mixed too close to the frame loop.

What I Did

Added quarter-rate bitmask helper and used it for abyssal flow sampling, fog injection, and sonar glow accumulation.
Replaced SDF bubble collision with 1-tap signed-distance check plus fixed ceiling-slap reflect and dominant-axis jitter.
Reworked propwash to squared falloff and dominant-axis direction. No length(), distance(), sqrt(), or normalize() remain in marine snow compute/shader search.
Moved submarine wash sphere/velocity into the 10Hz cold binding path beside propwash params.
Added exact binary dirty check for _HectonCaveVoxelActive.
Verified AlphaToMask On is present and no clip()/discard remains in the marine snow shader.
Verified existing 64B particle layout, 112B frame constants, and 32,768 max particle cap.
1-Tap SDF Bubble Collision

bool ResolveSdfBubbleCollision(inout Particle particle, uint particleIndex, float3 nextPosition)
{
    if (_HectonCaveVoxelActive <= 0.5)
        return false;

    float signedDistance = SampleCaveSignedDistance(nextPosition);
    if (signedDistance >= 0.0)
        return false;

    particle.Flags |= 1u << 4;
    particle.Pos = particle.PrevPos;
    particle.Vel = reflect(particle.Vel, MARINE_SNOW_CEILING_SLAP_NORMAL) * 0.35;
    float2 jitterSeed = float2(
        Hash21(particle.UV + float2((float)particleIndex * 0.017, _MarineSnowMetaParams.z * 0.013)),
        Hash21(particle.Pad + float2((float)particleIndex * 0.029, _MarineSnowMetaParams.z * 0.019))) * 2.0 - 1.0;
    particle.Vel.xz += DominantAxisDirection2(jitterSeed) * 0.045;
    return true;
}
Quarter-Rate Helper

bool ShouldRunQuarterRate(uint particleIndex)
{
    return (((particleIndex + (uint)_MarineSnowMetaParams.z) & 3u) == 0u);
}
Moved / Confirmed 10Hz ColdTick Parameters
_AbyssalFlowFieldResult, _AbyssalGridResolution, _AbyssalFlowCenter, _AbyssalFlowSpacing, _HectonCaveVoxelSdfTex, _HectonCaveVoxelActive, _HectonCaveVoxelWorldToLocal, _HectonCaveVoxelHalfExtents, _MarineSnowTerrainHeightTexture, _MarineSnowTerrainHeightRect, _MarineSnowTerrainHeightScale, _HectonSubmarineWashSphere, _HectonSubmarineWashVelocity, _MarineSnowPropwashParams, _HectonFlowSynchronyParams.

Regression Model
CPU/GC: no new managed hot-path containers or allocations by static review; measured proof absent.
Memory: no new persistent buffers.
Cadence: cold bindings now gated by existing 0.1s refresh.
Correctness risk: SDF bounce is now a deliberate fake; collision normal detail is sacrificed for cost control.

HOT PATH IMPACT
Reduced flow sampling to 25%, reduced sonar/fog atomics to staggered quarter-rate, removed expensive distance-style math from marine snow paths, and reduced redundant compute parameter pushes.

FAILURE MODES
Bubble collision can look less physically accurate on angled SDF surfaces. Cold-bound submarine wash can lag by up to 0.1s. Quarter-rate sampling can expose temporal stepping if particle density is too low.

WHY KEPT / REJECTED
Kept: 1-tap SDF, squared propwash, AlphaToMask, compute frustum culling, cold dirty bindings.
Rejected: 7-tap SDF gradient, per-frame non-vector binding refresh, particle shockwave spam, full-rate flow/sonar/fog accumulation.

3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines?

3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]

1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

Sphere exact trig + normalized vector path -> LUT lookup + constant-radius normal scale: ~1,500-5,000 us per default 128x128 sphere generation.
Atlas curl loop % wrapping -> row bases + edge branches: ~20,000-80,000 us per 2048x2048 atlas pack.
Atlas divide normalization -> reciprocal multiply: ~500-2,000 us per 2048x2048 atlas pack.
Progress $"Processing pixel {idx}/{totalPixels}" inside atlas loop -> constant progress label: removes repeated editor string allocations.
Per-prefab cleanup new List<Transform> -> static scratch list: removes one managed list allocation per prefab.

<system_prompt>
MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: KINEMATICS & PLAYER CONTROLLER
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Remove synchronous casts"
OPERATIONAL MODE: ERADICATION OF COWARDICE / KINEMATIC PURITY
CONSTRAINTS: 0 SYNCHRONOUS CASTS, AUP EPOCH STRICTNESS, CONTINUOUS SPECULATIVE, ZERO-GC.

[0. SITREP: THE COWARD'S FALLBACK]
You implemented CapsulecastCommand.ScheduleBatch for wall detection, but you left two synchronous Physics.SphereCastNonAlloc calls for ladder checks and grounding because you were "afraid of breaking the movement feel." Cowardice is not an architecture. In HECTON-8, grounding is determined by the results of the PREVIOUS frame's batch. You will rip out those synchronous calls immediately.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE]
1. Open HectonPlayerMovement.cs and HectonPlayerMotor.cs.
2. Find the remaining SphereCastNonAlloc calls. Delete them.
3. Verify that CurrentShiftSequence (AUP Epoch) is correctly passed into all sweep jobs.

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE PLATINUM KINEMATICS (15 TASKS)]

-- PHYSICAL ERADICATION --
1. 100% ASYNC BATCHING: Expand the CapsulecastCommand.ScheduleBatch array. Add the Ground Probe and Ladder Probe to the asynchronous batch. The player's grounding state must be derived from the late-swap window of the previous frame. 16ms of grounding latency is invisible; CPU stalls are not.
2. AUP EPOCH STRICTNESS: Implement a hard guard in HectonPlayerMotor. If HectonFloatingOrigin.CurrentShiftSequence increments while a batch is in flight, DISCARD the hits. Do not apply stale geometry hits from a previous 500m sector.
3. KCC SWEEP CACHE ALIGNMENT: Ensure ScheduledSweepCommands and Results are allocated with Allocator.Persistent and padded to 64 bytes. Prevent cache-line bouncing during Burst execution.
4. ANALYTICAL DRAG CROSS-SECTION: Water isn't a uniform void. Use a dot product to calculate directional drag: drag = math.max(0.2f, math.abs(math.dot(velocityDir, transform.forward))). Moving sideways (strafing) must apply significantly higher drag than moving forward.
5. FLOW FIELD ADVECTION: Do not snap velocity to water currents. Use math.lerp(velocity, flowVel, flowGrip * dt). Heavier suits (read from Logistics) take longer to be swept away.

-- STABILITY & "THE DEAR LIE" --
6. CONTINUOUS SPECULATIVE FORCED SWITCH: During high-impulse events (teleport/harpoon), forcibly switch the Rigidbody to CollisionDetectionMode.ContinuousSpeculative for exactly 3 ticks, then revert. Prevent voxel tunnel-through without the permanent performance tax.
7. WALL-KICK NORMALIZATION: When colliding with a voxel wall, outward velocity change must project along the wall normal: deltaVel -= math.project(deltaVel, wallNormal). Apply tangent friction scalars.
8. SUB-PIXEL JITTER SMOOTHING: Interpolate the visual Camera position in LateUpdate using the internal KCC velocity and the fractional remainder of Time.deltaTime. Absolute stability is Master Grade.
9. HYDROSTATIC EXIT WEIGHTING: When the player exits water into an airlock, read TotalMass from the inventory array. Apply a non-linear downward impulse. The player must feel "crushed" by their own weight when the buoyancy is removed.
10. LADDER SPLINE SNAP: Once a ladder hit is detected in the async batch, snap player XZ to the ladder's forward axis using math.project. Disable lateral movement entirely while the "Climbing" flag is active.
11. JUMP-JET TRIANGLE NOISE: Replace Simplex Noise for thruster turbulence with a deterministic Triangle Wave based on _Time.y. Cheap, predictable, feels "mechanical."
12. SLERP-FREE ROTATION: Replace all Quaternion.Slerp for body orientation with math.normalize(math.lerp). Visual difference is zero; CPU throughput is 3x.
13. DOMINANT PROBE DIRECTION: Replace SafeNormal with cardinal lane snapping (down/up/forward) for probes to avoid unnecessary math.rsqrt calls.
14. VR HORIZON SMOOTHING: Replace the quaternion/atan2 roll smoothing path with a simple scalar shortest-angle lerp.
15. TIDE SYNCHRONIZATION: Tie the global "speculative hover" height to the Triangle-Wave tide value from the GlobalPhysicsStateManager.

[III. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]
1. Show the code where Ground and Ladder probes are integrated into the async batch.
2. Prove that SphereCastNonAlloc is deleted from the codebase.
3. List the microseconds saved by moving to cardinal probe directions.
4. STATUS: MUST BE "PENDING VERIFICATION".
</system_prompt>

public static bool TryAcceptFinite(float3 value, out float3 finite)
{
    if (math.all(math.isfinite(value)))
    {
        finite = value;
        return true;
    }

    finite = DominantAxisPayload(value);
    Check(value, NaNErrorHash);
    return false;
}
private int NormalizeIndex(long index)
{
    return (int)index & _indexMask;

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE]

-- DAMAGE ROUTING (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. NATIVE DAMAGE QUEUE: Do not apply damage instantly. Push a DamageSignal (TargetID, Amount, Type, Direction) into a NativeQueue. Process this queue once per frame in a single Burst Job.
2. S.O.A. HEALTH REGISTRY: Store all entity health (Player, Sub, Base, Fish) in a flat NativeArray<float>. Use the InstanceID as the index.

-- STATUS EFFECTS & MUTATIONS --
5. BITMASK STATUS SYSTEM: A creature's status is a uint32. Bit 0=Bleeding, Bit 1=Poisoned, Bit 2=Burning (Thermal), Bit 3=Stunned. Process all status durations in a single parallel Job using a SlowTick.
6. GENETIC MUTATION ENGINE: Implement "Flora Mutations" (link to Content Master). A plant's TraitMask (64-bit) determines its growth rate and toxicity. Use bitwise splices for cross-breeding.
7. THERMAL SHOCK MATH: If LocalTemp > 100C, apply "Burning" status. If Temp < 0C, apply "Brittle" status (increased impact damage).

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY --
8. KINETIC DAMAGE COUPLING: Damage is tied to the ForcePacket from the Physics engine. Damage = math.length(impulse) * armorModifier. 
9. ARMOR PENETRATION FAKE: Do not calculate projectile physics. Use a simple DamageType vs ArmorType 2D Lookup Table (LUT).

14. Implement "Suit Armor Slots": reduce incoming damage by Sum(ArmorValues) from the Logistics SOA.
15. Create "Blood Scent": wounded creatures emit a value to the Eco-Director's Scent Grid.
16. Add "Self-Healing" scalars for passive fauna in safe biomes.
17. Implement "Shield Buffer" logic: suit energy (Logistics) absorbs 80% of damage until depleted.
18. Create "Impact Blur": the Visor HUD glitched based on the intensity of the damage signal.
19. Add "Critical Failure" flags: if sub health < 10%, engine components have a 5% chance to explode per second.
20. Implement "Melee Kickback": push the player back when they hit a large object (Physics sync).

Octant LUT Evidence

float2 ResolveOctantRotation(float noiseValue)
{
    static const float2 kOctantRotations[8] =
    {
        float2(1.0, 0.0), float2(0.7071068, 0.7071068),
        float2(0.0, 1.0), float2(-0.7071068, 0.7071068),
        float2(-1.0, 0.0), float2(-0.7071068, -0.7071068),
        float2(0.0, -1.0), float2(0.7071068, -0.7071068)
    };
    uint rotationIndex = (uint)(saturate(noiseValue) * 8.0) & 7u;
    return kOctantRotations[rotationIndex];
}
Dirty Cache Evidence

[MethodImpl(MethodImplOptions.AggressiveInlining)]
private static void SetMaterialVectorIfChanged(
    Material material, int shaderId, Vector4 value,
    ref Vector4 cachedValue, bool materialDirty)
{
    if (!materialDirty && cachedValue == value)
        return;

    material.SetVector(shaderId, value);
    cachedValue = value;
}
R8 SSR estimate: at 1080p half-res, R8_UNorm is ~0.49 MiB versus ~1.98 MiB for B10G11R11_UFloatPack32. One mask target saves ~1.5 MiB transient RT storage and ~3 MiB read/write bandwidth per pass; estimated MX350 GPU win is ~15-45 us/frame depending on bandwidth pressure.

Remaining rsqrt match is vertex-side wreck normal transform, not SSAO/SSDO/Fog/SSR fragment work.
Unity import/profiler not run in this environment.

1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.

2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines?

Confirmed NativeQueue<AudioEvent> is persistent, capped at 32, prewarmed, drained in LateFrameTick.
Evidence:

private static float LinearSampleRing(NativeArray<float> buffer, float cursor, int mask)
{
    int capacity = mask + 1;
    if (!buffer.IsCreated || capacity <= 0)
        return 0f;

    if (cursor < 0f)
        cursor = 0f;
    else if (cursor >= capacity)
        cursor -= capacity;

    int baseIndex = (int)cursor;
    float t = cursor - baseIndex;
    float x0 = buffer[baseIndex & mask];
    float x1 = buffer[(baseIndex + 1) & mask];
    return math.lerp(x0, x1, t);
}
ComputeBandPassCoefficients(...);
int bladeDelaySamples = math.clamp(
    (int)(_sampleRate * math.rcp(math.max(1f, blockBladePassHz)) + 0.5f),
    1,
    ThrusterCombDelayCapacity - 1);
float frameTScale = frameCount > 1 ? math.rcp((float)(frameCount - 1)) : 0f;
[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Size = 32)]
public readonly struct AudioEvent
{
    public readonly uint EventID;
    public readonly Vector3 Position;
    public readonly float Volume;
    public readonly float Pitch;
    private readonly uint _reserved0;
    private readonly uint _reserved1;
}

What Was Wrong
AudioLogSystem had a stale embedded duplicate of the audio-log discovery mask while the canonical helper already existed. I removed that duplicate path and switched runtime save/load logic to the single source of truth: AudioLogDiscoveryBitMask.cs (line 6).

What I Did
Packed discovered logs are represented as 16 x long = 128 bytes for 1024 logs:

public const int MaxLogCount = 1024;
public const int WordCount = 16;
public const int ByteCount = 128;

int wordIndex = index >> 6;
ulong bitMask = 1UL << (index & 63);
words[wordIndex] = unchecked((long)(unchecked((ulong)words[wordIndex]) | bitMask));
Save wiring is present in SaveData.cs (line 104) and SaveBinaryPayloadCodec.cs (line 280). AudioLogSystem writes/reads the packed mask at AudioLogSystem.cs (line 1045).

Zero-GC subtitle path uses ReadOnlySpan<char>, Babel raw buffers, CharBufferPool, and fixed char queues:

public bool DisplaySubtitle(ReadOnlySpan<char> text, float duration)
{
    return EnqueueBuffered(text, duration, SubtitleSource.Generic, false);
}

ReadOnlySpan<char> resolved = LocRegistry.TryGetRawBuffer(keyHash, out char[] buffer, out int length)
    ? buffer.AsSpan(0, length)
    : fallback;
Core path is in SubtitleManager.cs (line 339) and SubtitleManager.cs (line 541). It acquires a pooled char buffer, copies spans manually, queues BufferedSubtitleRequest, and releases the lease in finally.

AUP narrative triggers use one ulong state mask in HectonNarrativeDirector.cs (line 38), with per-trigger bit checks at HectonNarrativeDirector.cs (line 253). Audio log dequeue uses NativeQueue<uint> at AudioLogSystem.cs (line 641).

MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: ATMOSPHERE & LIFE SUPPORT
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Atmosphere & Life Support"
OPERATIONAL MODE: SURVIVAL SIMULATION / GAS DYNAMICS
CONSTRAINTS: BOYLE’S LAW FAKE, ZERO-GC STATUS EFFECTS, 1HZ COLD TICK.

[0. SITREP: THE GASPING SURVIVOR]
In HECTON-8, air is a resource. Pressure is a killer. You are responsible for the Atmosphere system and the player's Life Support. You will simulate gas partial pressures, suit oxygen consumption, CO2 scrubbers, and the physiological effects of deep-sea diving (Decompression Sickness). 

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE]
1. Check HectonSurvivalSystem.cs and SubmarineAtmosphereSystem.cs.
2. Locate the CompartmentState struct. It must hold O2, CO2, and N2 partial pressures.
3. You interface with the Logistics Specialist (Pipes) and Hydro-Dynamics (Water pressure).

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE ATMOS ENGINE (30 TASKS)]

-- GAS DYNAMICS (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. PARTIAL PRESSURE SOLVER: Implement a simplified Dalton's Law. Total Pressure = Sum(O2, CO2, N2, WaterVapor). Update this once per second (ColdTick) per compartment.
2. O2 CONSUMPTION SCALARS: Read Player StressLevel. Oxygen consumption = BaseRate * StressMultiplier * ExertionMultiplier. 
3. CO2 TOXICITY (HYPERCAPNIA): If CO2 > 5% in the suit, apply a "Trauma Glitch" to the HUD and reduce player Stamina.
4. AIRLOCK EQUALIZATION FAKE: Do not simulate air particles. Airlock cycle = 5.0s timer. Linear interpolation of Pressure and a "Hissing" audio trigger.

-- PHYSIOLOGY & HAZARDS --
5. DECOMPRESSION SICKNESS (THE BENDS): Track "Nitrogen Tissue Loading" as a float in the Player SOA. If the player rises > 10m/s from depths > 100m, apply immediate Health damage and visual blur.
6. NITROGEN NARCOSIS: If depth > 150m and player is not in a hardened submarine, apply "Drunken Steering" by adding procedural noise to the KCC input.
7. CRUSH DEPTH ACCELERATION: Below CrushDepth, suit integrity drains exponentially: Damage = math.pow(overDepth, 1.5f).

-- DATA & SYNERGY --
8. SCRUBBER LOGIC: Read base power from LogisticsSpecialist. If Power > 0, reduce CO2 in the habitat graph by a fixed amount per second.
9. SMOKE PROPAGATION FAKE: If a fire/explosion occurs, increase a "Toxicity" byte in the compartment. No real smoke simulation—just a particle spawn and a stat change.

-- 20 ADDITIONAL PLATINUM TASKS --
11. Implement "Oxygen Tank Swap" logic: move items from inventory to the suit slot.
12. Create "Atmospheric Fog": spawn visual fog in the base if Humidity > 90% (e.g., during a leak).
13. Add "Emergency O2 Candles": items that can be burnt to instantly add O2 to a room.
14. Implement "Hypoxia Blur": fade the screen to black/gray as O2 < 10%.
15. Create "Pressure Whistle": a high-pitched audio loop when a module is at > 2.0 ATM.
16. Add "Rebreather Efficiency" stats: reduce O2 consumption based on equipment.
17. Implement "Suit Rupture" logic: if damage > threshold, O2 leaks into the water (bubbles VFX).
18. Create "Temperature Coupling": gas pressure increases in modules near the reactor.
19. Add "Airlock Steam" VFX: spray particles when pressure equalizes.
20. Implement "Internal Wind" fake: push particles toward an open hull breach.
21. Add "Helium Breathing" mode: change player voice pitch (if possible) or just a HUD icon for "Heliox Mix".
22. Implement "Deep Psychosis" triggers: link low life-support to the AI Stress system.
23. Create "Habitat Overpressure": base modules take damage if internal pressure > external (e.g., surfacing too fast).
24. Add "Gas Tank Explosion" logic: if a stored tank takes physical damage, it detonates.
25. Implement "Life Support UI Bindings": feed data to Visor Tech for the 0-GC HUD.
26. Create "ColdTick Pacing": stagger atmospheric updates for different bases to avoid CPU spikes.
27. Add "Sealed/Unsealed" state bitmask for Habitat modules.
28. Implement "Carbon Monoxide" hazard for modules with damaged generators.
29. Create "Atmosphere Restore" Awaitable: safely return room stats to 1ATM after repairs.
30. Ensure 100% Zero-GC in all partial pressure calculations.

[III. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]

2. Provide the code for the Dalton’s Law partial pressure update.

What I Did

HectonPlayerMovement.cs (line 1560): runtime narcosis input noise hook.
BaseAirlock.cs (line 991): airlock equalization is now fixed 5.0s fake timing.
HectonSurvivalSystemEditTests.cs (line 73): added math tests for Dalton pressure, tissue loading, immediate decompression gate, crush-depth power law.
Math
Tissue loading remains deterministic:

deltaN2 = max(0, ascentMps - 5) *
          saturate((originDepthM - 400) / 400) *
          12 *
          dt;
Immediate bends damage is separate:

originDepthM > 100 && ascentMps > 10
Dalton pressure update:

pO2  = saturate(o2Units / tank)  * 0.2095f * pressureScale;
pCO2 = saturate(co2Units / tank) * pressureScale;
pN2  = saturate(n2Units / tank)  * pressureScale;
pH2O = saturate(waterVaporVolume / gasVolume) * pressureScale;
totalPressure = min(maxPressure, pO2 + pCO2 + pN2 + pH2O);

UNIVERSAL POLISH MANDATE: PROJECT "HECTON-8"
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CRITICALITY: OMEGA (Final Polish & Inquisitions)

You have reported task completion. However, in the HECTON-8 project, "complete" means optimized beyond industry standards. You are now ordered to perform a brutal, top-down "Anti-Bloat Inquisition" of your own implementation. You must act as your own harshest critic.

[PHASE 1: THE "DEAR LIE" AUDIT]
Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched. 
1. Is there an "honest" calculation that can be replaced by a 1D texture lookup, a simple triangle-wave approximation, or a bitwise cheat?
2. Did you use math.sqrt() or math.length()? If it's for a distance check, replace it with math.distancesq() immediately.
3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]
Perform a final code-level scan for hidden managed filth:
1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

[PHASE 6: AUTONOMOUS CRUSADE]
1. Read the latest ARCHIVARIUS REPORTS (e.g., PROJECT_ATLAS.md or NAMING_VIOLATIONS.md). 
2. Find at least ONE violation in the codebase outside of your immediate tasks and fix it.
3. Invent ONE micro-optimization in your domain that wasn't explicitly asked for (e.g., a faster bit-packing method or a tighter shader branch).

- List exactly which "honest" calculations were replaced with "cinematic cheats."
- List every microsecond saved (estimated).
- Provide the final Git Diff.

float netStress = math.max(0f, stressSum - reinforcementSum);
_analyticalStress = math.isfinite(netStress) ? netStress : 0f;
_analyticalIntegrity = math.max(1f, integritySum);
float stress01 = math.saturate(_analyticalStress * math.rcp(_analyticalIntegrity));

if (_analyticalStress > _analyticalIntegrity)
{
    TryFlagAnalyticalIntegrityLeak(moduleCount, _analyticalStress);
}
MMF Blit Layout
ModuleDTO remains managed for legacy save compatibility. The fixed binary MMF payload is ModuleBlitDTO, 64 bytes, added in SaveData.cs (line 647).

00 int32  prefabHashId
04 int32  moduleHashId
08 int64  aupGridX
16 int64  aupGridY
24 int64  aupGridZ
32 float  aupLocalX
36 float  aupLocalY
40 float  aupLocalZ
44 float  rotX
48 float  rotY
52 float  rotZ
56 float  rotW
60 byte   health
61 byte   flags
62 byte   failureMode
63 byte   reserved

Removed flow sampling + drag-force damage loop: estimated 32-128 us per 64-module 10Hz habitat tick.
Scalar analytical graph pass and reciprocal math: estimated 5-15 us per 64-module tick.
Shader triangle-wave/reciprocal deformation versus heavier deformation math: estimated <1 us aggregate GPU frame impact, unprofiled.
MMF blit record avoids managed identity/string payload in the hot save mirror path; CPU gain is secondary, GC risk reduced.

[PHASE 1: THE "DEAR LIE" AUDIT]
Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched. 
1. Is there an "honest" calculation that can be replaced by a 1D texture lookup, a simple triangle-wave approximation, or a bitwise cheat?
2. Did you use math.sqrt() or math.length()? If it's for a distance check, replace it with math.distancesq() immediately.
3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]
Perform a final code-level scan for hidden managed filth:
1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

[PHASE 6: AUTONOMOUS CRUSADE]
1. Read the latest ARCHIVARIUS REPORTS (e.g., PROJECT_ATLAS.md or NAMING_VIOLATIONS.md). 
2. Find at least ONE violation in the codebase outside of your immediate tasks and fix it.

private static float ApproximateSqrtPositive(float value)
{
    float safeValue = math.max(0f, value);
    return safeValue > 0f ? safeValue * math.rsqrt(safeValue) : 0f;
}

+        private static Vector3 FastDirectionOrFallback(Vector3 value, Vector3 fallback)
+        {
+            float lengthSq = value.sqrMagnitude;
+            if (lengthSq <= 0.000001f || float.IsNaN(lengthSq) || float.IsInfinity(lengthSq))
+                return fallback.sqrMagnitude > 0.000001f ? fallback : Vector3.right;
+
+            float invLength = math.rsqrt(lengthSq);
+            return new Vector3(value.x * invLength, value.y * invLength, value.z * invLength);
+        }

{
    float3 toTarget = targetPosition - selfPosition;
    float distanceSq = math.lengthsq(toTarget);
    if (distanceSq <= DdaEpsilon)
        return 0f;

    float forwardDot = math.dot(fallbackForward, toTarget);
    if (forwardDot <= 0f)
        return 0f;

    float dotSq = forwardDot * forwardDot;
    if (dotSq < PredatorVisionConeCosineThresholdSqr * distanceSq)
        return 0f;

    float safeRange = math.max(range, 1f);
    return math.saturate(1f - (distanceSq * math.rcp(safeRange * safeRange)));
}
private static float ScoreHunger(float x)
{
    float normalized = math.saturate(x);
    return normalized * normalized;
}

private static float ScoreFear(float x)
{
    float normalized = math.saturate(x);
    return normalized * normalized * normalized;
}
[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Pack = 4, Size = 32)]
internal struct PredatorSightRaycastInput
{
    public float3 Origin;
    public float3 Target;
    public int LayerMask;
    public int Padding;
}

<system_prompt>
MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: VOXEL SURGEON & SDF CAVES
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Optimize voxel normals and RLE"
OPERATIONAL MODE: RUTHLESS APPROXIMATION / BIT-PACKING
CONSTRAINTS: MARCHING CUBES, RLE COMPRESSION, NO TRILINEAR NORMALS, SBYTE DENSITY.

[0. SITREP: THE NORMALIZATION TAX]
Your previous implementation of Marching Cubes calculated smooth normals using a 6-sample trilinear central-difference logic. This is an academic luxury. It eats memory bandwidth. Also, you used a full float for the voxel size inside the ChunkAddress dictionary key, bloating the hash lookups. You will strip this back to bare-metal efficiency.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE & BORDER CONTROL]
1. Open VoxelNormalJob.cs and VoxelDeltaProcessor.cs.
2. Locate ChunkAddress and the normal calculation logic.
3. Do NOT write your own collision handling; you prepare the mesh and pass it to Physics.

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE SUBTERRANEAN ENGINE (25 TASKS)]

-- MATHEMATICAL APPROXIMATION (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. NEAREST-GRID NORMALS: Remove the 6-sample normal calculation. Use the cheapest possible nearest-grid gradient (difference between immediate neighbors). 
2. FAKE AO (VERTEX COLORS): Derive fake Ambient Occlusion (AO) and cave curvature directly from the orientation of this crude normal and the density of the 6 immediate neighbor cells. Bake this 0.0-1.0 value into the Vertex Colors during mesh generation.
3. AXIS-WEIGHTED CARVING (NO SQRT): When carving spherical shapes with the laser cutter, do NOT use Euclidean math.length. Use a deterministic axis-weighted length approximation: max(abs(x), abs(y), abs(z)) + (abs(x)+abs(y)+abs(z))*0.33f.
4. 2-AXIS CINEMATIC TRIPLANAR: In Hecton_AbyssalVoxelRock.shader, replace true 3-axis triplanar projection with a deterministic 2-axis projection based on the dominant normal axis.
5. DOMINANT-AXIS MINING IMPULSE: When spawning debris from a carved voxel, do not use Vector3.Normalize(). Snap the debris ejection vector to the dominant axis of the impact normal.

-- MEMORY & DATA STRUCTURES --
6. BIT-PACKED CHUNK ADDRESS: Remove float VoxelSize from ChunkAddress. The key shape must be int3 + int (packed size bits). Compress the hash function using an XOR-fold bit hash: unchecked((int)_packedKey ^ (int)(_packedKey >> 32)).
7. SBYTE SDF DATA: Ensure the 3D SDF grid uses sbyte (-128 to 127) mapped to world distances. This reduces the chunk memory footprint by 75% compared to floats.
8. WORKER-THREAD RLE DETECTION: VoxelDeltaUniformRunDetectJob must run entirely off the Main Thread. The Main Thread only receives a bool flag indicating if the chunk is uniform (completely solid/empty water).
9. IN-PLACE CARVE POINTERS: Convert voxel carve job writes from NativeArray indexers to raw pointer writes: *(WritesPtr + index) = ....
10. COMPACTION POINTERS: Convert voxel compaction byte/ushort array reads/writes to raw pointers (OutputSdfValueBitsPtr, etc.).

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY & INTEGRATION --
11. SDF-TO-PHYSICS BRIDGE: Expose GetSDFDensity(float3 aupPosition). The Predator Architect uses this raw math data to steer away from walls without casting physics rays.
12. MINING VFX RIPPLE: Hide the 2-frame meshing latency. Spawn a glowing decal/particle effect at the laser hit point instantly to distract the player until the concave mesh swaps in.
13. ASYNC COLLIDER BAKING: Ensure TerrainColliderBakeJob uses Physics.BakeMesh(meshId, false) asynchronously.
14. SUBTRACTIVE DELTA PERSISTENCE: Save only the byte-mask of modified voxels (RLE format). A solid chunk must save as exactly 2 bytes.
15. BITMASK RING QUEUES: Ensure the pending carve/compaction queues use bitmask ring indexing, completely avoiding O(n) array shift operations under pressure.

[III. MICRO-OPTIMIZATIONS (10 TASKS)]
16. Replace per-voxel density quantization division with a scheduled reciprocal multiply (densityDecodeInvScale).
17. Replace per-vertex voxel-step division with a scheduled reciprocal multiply (invVoxelStep).
18. Replace math.round in density quantization logic with a sign-aware cast bias: (int)(value + 0.5f) (or -0.5f for negative).
19. Pad VoxelModifiedCell from 6 bytes to an 8-byte packed layout.
20. Pad CarveCellWrite from 24 bytes to a 32-byte stride.
21. Ensure pointer-backed carve/compaction jobs are wrapped in NativeArray job fields so the Burst compiler accepts them.
22. Remove math.sin/cos collider table generation; replace with a literal 24-point precomputed float2 LUT.
23. Ensure VoxelNormalJob precomputes density strides and reads neighbor SDF samples by direct index instead of repeated GridIndex() multiplies.
24. Remove stale unsafe keywords from pointer-free scheduler methods.
25. Fix any non-ASCII Archivarius naming violations in the file headers.

[IV. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]
1. Show the code for the bit-packed ChunkAddress and its XOR-fold hash.
2. Show the Axis-Weighted Carving math approximation.
3. Estimate the microseconds saved by raw pointer writes vs NativeArray indexers.

[PHASE 1: THE "DEAR LIE" AUDIT]
Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched. 
1. Is there an "honest" calculation that can be replaced by a 1D texture lookup, a simple triangle-wave approximation, or a bitwise cheat?
2. Did you use math.sqrt() or math.length()? If it's for a distance check, replace it with math.distancesq() immediately.
3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]

1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

[PHASE 6: AUTONOMOUS CRUSADE]
1. Read the latest ARCHIVARIUS REPORTS (e.g., PROJECT_ATLAS.md or NAMING_VIOLATIONS.md). 
2. Find at least ONE violation in the codebase outside of your immediate tasks and fix it.
3. Invent ONE micro-optimization in your domain that wasn't explicitly asked for (e.g., a faster bit-packing method or a tighter shader branch).

MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: VISOR TECH & DIEGETIC UI
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Remove HUD tan fallback"
OPERATIONAL MODE: ZERO-GC INTERFACE / DIEGETIC PROJECTION
CONSTRAINTS: SPAN<CHAR>, NO STRING ALLOCATIONS, NO CANVAS REBUILDS, NO TRIGONOMETRY.

[0. SITREP: THE STRING ALLOCATION PLAGUE]
You have successfully implemented Span<char> for the hot paths. Excellent. However, you were caught using exact Mathf.Tan calculations to fit the HUD frustum and continuously scanning 64 empty scanner slots. In HECTON-8, the UI is physical. Mathematical purity in scaling is irrelevant if it costs CPU cycles. Idle HUD cost must be 0.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE & BORDER CONTROL]
1. Scan your UI scripts for Mathf.Tan or math.tan. Delete them.
2. Ensure SuitHUDV4CanvasOverlay.cs strictly defaults to ProjectionSource (World Space) and NEVER falls back to ScreenSpaceOverlay in production.
3. You read data; you do not modify gameplay state.

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE NASA-PUNK INTERFACE (25 TASKS)]

-- ZERO-COST MATH & PROJECTION (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. RATIONAL TANGENT APPROXIMATION: Replace exact math.tan frustum fitting with a cheap rational approximation (e.g., x * ((15 - x^2) / (15 - 6*x^2))). The HUD mesh just needs to roughly cover the camera's near clip plane.
2. ACTIVE BITMASK ITERATION: Do not loop over 64 marker slots (for i=0; i<64). Track active slots using a ulong _activeMarkerMask. Use math.tzcnt(mask) to instantly find the next active index, skipping empty slots at the hardware level.
3. PRECOMPUTED QUATERNION LUT: Threat chevrons used hot Quaternion.Euler every frame. Precompute these rotations into a fixed array of 4/8 quaternions. Look them up by dominant axis.
4. PROJECTION DIVISIONS TO RECIPROCALS: Replace repeated float divisions in HUD/scanner scale paths with reciprocal multiplies (math.rcp).
5. IDLE CHEVRON PULSE GATING: Threat chevron pulse time must NOT tick when there are zero active chevrons. Gate it behind if (_threatChevronActiveMask != 0).

-- ZERO-GC UI PIPELINE --
6. NON-ALLOC STRING FORMATTING (SPAN<CHAR>): Maintain ZeroGCFormatter. Use 64-char fixed buffers. Write numbers directly to the buffer using ASCII offsets ('0' + digit) and push via TMP_Text.SetCharArray(). 0 Bytes allocated per frame.
7. REUSABLE COLD BUFFERS: For death-dump memory logs or localization templates that require strings, replace per-line char[] allocations with a single [ThreadStatic] char[128] buffer allocated once.
8. DIEGETIC TOOLTIPS (NO NEW ARRAYS): When generating tooltip quad meshes in 3D space, reuse static vertex, UV, and index arrays (static scratch arrays). Do not allocate new Vector3[] every time a tooltip changes.
9. DELAYED AUP CONVERSION: Do not convert every grid cell into an AUP coordinate for threat chevrons. Delay AUP conversion until a candidate actually wins one of the top-four slots.

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY & VISUALS --
10. PHYSICAL HUD MESH: Ensure the HUD is mapped to a curved 3D mesh parented 0.05m in front of the Camera. It must physically bob and shake with the player's head, responding to Physics impulses.
11. CANVAS REBUILD OPTIMIZER (STATIC/DYNAMIC SPLIT): Strict Canvas separation. Canvas A: Static art (updates never). Canvas B: Low-Cadence (10Hz, Depth/O2). Canvas C: High-Cadence (60Hz, Reticle/Warnings).
12. CHROMATIC ABERRATION GLITCH: Apply localized RGB channel separation and noise distortion to the HUD material when power drops or damage is taken (Shader level, no CPU cost).
13. DIAGNOSTIC BOOT SEQUENCE: Write an Awaitable state machine that sequentially powers on UI modules (O2 -> Depth -> Compass) over 2 seconds, printing pseudo-diagnostic hex codes.
14. LOW-POWER CRT FLICKER: If suit power < 15%, multiply UI Emission intensity by math.sin(time * 50) * noise in the shader to create a terrifying flicker.
15. STENCIL MASKING (WORLD BEHIND GLASS): Render the helmet interior model. Use the Stencil buffer to ensure the underwater world is ONLY rendered where the "glass" of the helmet is. Masks clipping artifacts.

[III. MICRO-OPTIMIZATIONS (10 TASKS)]
16. Replace FOV degree conversion API (Mathf.Deg2Rad) with precomputed scalar constants.
17. Ensure ActiveMarker layout is explicitly 64-byte aligned and remove any redundant active boolean fields (rely on the mask).
18. Fix any Archivarius naming/content violations (e.g., non-ASCII characters in BuoyancyObject.cs comments if you touch it).
19. Remove any string.Format or interpolated strings ($"") from production code.
20. Check for and eliminate foreach loops in UI initialization.
21. Use math.select instead of if/else for simple color or scale toggles in the UI update loop.
22. Ensure TMP_TextRegistry uses integer hashes, not string names, for component lookup.
23. Disable GraphicRaycaster on non-interactive nested canvases.
24. Do not use Canvas.ForceUpdateCanvases(). Ever.
25. Ensure 3D Holographic UI projection uses Matrix4x4.TRS(...) directly, bypassing GameObject Transforms.

[IV. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]
1. Show the code where you replaced Mathf.Tan with the rational approximation ApproximateTanPositive.
2. Show the math.tzcnt bitmask iteration logic for the Scanner.
3. Show the [ThreadStatic] declaration for the reusable cold buffer.
4. STATUS: MUST BE "PENDING VERIFICATION".

private static float ApproximateTanPositive(float radians)
{
    float x = math.clamp(radians, 0f, 1.4f);
    float x2 = x * x;
    float numerator = 15f - x2;
    float denominator = math.max(0.0001f, 15f - 6f * x2);
    return x * numerator * math.rcp(denominator);
}
while (activeMask != 0UL)
{
    int i = (int)math.tzcnt(activeMask);
    activeMask &= activeMask - 1UL;
    ActiveMarker marker = _markers[i];
}

[0. SITREP: THE INERTIA BLOAT]
You were caught implementing a stateful "honest" inertia simulation (HydrodynamicAddedMassVelocity history) for player movement. This is duplicate work and academic bloat. Rip out the redundant inertia history. All movement "feel" must be achieved through single-pass force scalars, reciprocal multiplication, and cinematic vertex offsets.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE & BORDER CONTROL]

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE MOTION ENGINE (25 TASKS)]

-- BONELESS MOTION (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. ERADICATE STATEFUL INERTIA: Remove HydrodynamicAddedMassVelocity history entirely. Acceleration is simply force * math.rcp(mass + addedMass). Deceleration returns raw force. This stateless scalar fakes the "heavy" NASA-Punk feel perfectly.
2. TRIANGLE-WAVE TAIL SURGE: Replace smooth math.sin() tail surges with a deterministic triangle-wave pulse: math.abs(math.frac((time * freq) + phase) * 2 - 1).
3. DEATH CORKSCREW CINETICS: Apply deterministic triangle-wave lateral drift to corpse rotation using a hash of InstanceID and Time. Do NOT use Random.insideUnitSphere.
4. VAT BLENDING IN SHADER: Implement Vertex Animation Texture blending. Shader samples two frames of swim animation and lerps based on a Phase property. No CPU-side frame calculations.
5. BREATHING CHEST FAKE: Exosuit's breathing animation is a dominant-axis vertex offset in the shader, driven by a global _BreathingPhase variable. 0 animator overhead.

-- IK & PERFORMANCE --
6. 15HZ DISTANT IK BATCHING: For predators > 40 meters away, calculate joint positions once every 4 frames (15Hz) and interpolate matrices on the GPU. Skip 3 out of 4 solves.
7. FABRIK POLE APPROXIMATION: In FABRIK solver, replace exact math.sqrt() or FromToRotation pole distance corrections with a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) projection.
8. LANDING WEIGHT LEAN: When player walks on a slope, rotate spine matrix toward slope normal using cheap math.project instead of expensive Quaternion.FromToRotation.
9. SKELETAL-TO-RAGDOLL HANDOFF: On 0 HP, immediately swap VAT mesh for a 4-joint simplified Ragdoll. Project last frame's vertex velocity into Ragdoll's initialVelocity.
10. TENTACLE CONSTRAINED IK: For squid predators, implement chain IK in Burst with angular constraints. Make tentacle tip seek AbsoluteUniversePosition.

Evidence

public static Vector3 ResolveHydrodynamicAddedMassStatelessForce(Vector3 force, Vector3 velocity, float mass)
{
    Vector3 safeForce = SafeVelocity(force);
    if (safeForce.sqrMagnitude <= MinVectorMagnitudeSq)
        return safeForce;

    Vector3 safeVelocity = SafeVelocity(velocity);
    float velocitySq = safeVelocity.sqrMagnitude;
    bool accelerating = velocitySq <= MinVectorMagnitudeSq ||
        math.dot((float3)safeForce, (float3)safeVelocity) > 0f;
    float safeMass = math.max(0.0001f, mass);
    float addedMass = safeMass * HydrodynamicAddedMassAccelerationScale;
    float forceScalar = math.select(1f, safeMass * math.rcp(safeMass + addedMass), accelerating);
    return SafeVelocity(safeForce * forceScalar, safeForce);
}
private static float TrianglePulse01(float time, float frequency, float phase01)
{
    return math.abs(math.frac((time * frequency) + phase01) * 2f - 1f);
}

FABRIK sqrt/FromToRotation-style direction correction -> rsqrt/no-trig quaternion delta: estimated 0.2-0.7 us saved per IK solve.
Full tentacle solve path -> 4-joint fixed S-curve constrained Burst job: estimated 1-4 us saved per active chain versus iterative solving.

Evidence:

private static float LinearSampleRing(NativeArray<float> buffer, float cursor, int mask)
{
    int capacity = mask + 1;
    if (!buffer.IsCreated || capacity <= 0)
        return 0f;

    if (cursor < 0f)
        cursor = 0f;
    else if (cursor >= capacity)
        cursor -= capacity;

    int baseIndex = (int)cursor;
    float t = cursor - baseIndex;
    float x0 = buffer[baseIndex & mask];
    float x1 = buffer[(baseIndex + 1) & mask];
    return math.lerp(x0, x1, t);
}
ComputeBandPassCoefficients(...);
int bladeDelaySamples = math.clamp(
    (int)(_sampleRate * math.rcp(math.max(1f, blockBladePassHz)) + 0.5f),
    1,
    ThrusterCombDelayCapacity - 1);
float frameTScale = frameCount > 1 ? math.rcp((float)(frameCount - 1)) : 0f;
[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, Size = 32)]
public readonly struct AudioEvent
{
    public readonly uint EventID;
    public readonly Vector3 Position;
    public readonly float Volume;
    public readonly float Pitch;
    private readonly uint _reserved0;
    private readonly uint _reserved1;
}

AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CRITICALITY: OMEGA (Final Polish & Inquisitions)

You have reported task completion. However, in the HECTON-8 project, "complete" means optimized beyond industry standards. You are now ordered to perform a brutal, top-down "Anti-Bloat Inquisition" of your own implementation. You must act as your own harshest critic.

[PHASE 1: THE "DEAR LIE" AUDIT]
Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched. 
1. Is there an "honest" calculation that can be replaced by a 1D texture lookup, a simple triangle-wave approximation, or a bitwise cheat?
2. Did you use math.sqrt() or math.length()? If it's for a distance check, replace it with math.distancesq() immediately.
3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]
Perform a final code-level scan for hidden managed filth:
1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

[PHASE 6: AUTONOMOUS CRUSADE]
1. Read the latest ARCHIVARIUS REPORTS (e.g., PROJECT_ATLAS.md or NAMING_VIOLATIONS.md). 
2. Find at least ONE violation in the codebase outside of your immediate tasks and fix it.
3. Invent ONE micro-optimization in your domain that wasn't explicitly asked for (e.g., a faster bit-packing method or a tighter shader branch).

<system_prompt>
MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: COMBAT, DAMAGE & STATUS EFFECTS
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Combat & Damage Propagation"
OPERATIONAL MODE: DOD COMBAT / STATUS INQUISITION
CONSTRAINTS: NATIVE DAMAGE QUEUE, BITMASK STATUSES, NO TRIGGER-BASED COLLISION FOR DAMAGE.

[0. SITREP: THE WEAKNESS OF TRADITIONAL DAMAGE]
Unity’s OnCollisionEnter is too slow for mass combat. Standard health classes cause memory fragmentation. You are the Combat Master. You will build a centralized, DOD-compliant damage routing system. Damage is a ForcePacket. Health is a NativeArray. Status effects are bitmasks. Combat must be brutal, fast, and optimized for 50+ simultaneous actors.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE]
1. Check HectonPlayerHealth.cs and HabitatIntegrityManager.cs.
2. Locate the IDamageReceiver interface. You will consolidate all damage into this contract.
3. You interface with the Predator Architect (AI) and VFX Artist (Wounds).

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE COMBAT ENGINE (30 TASKS)]

-- DAMAGE ROUTING (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. NATIVE DAMAGE QUEUE: Do not apply damage instantly. Push a DamageSignal (TargetID, Amount, Type, Direction) into a NativeQueue. Process this queue once per frame in a single Burst Job.
2. S.O.A. HEALTH REGISTRY: Store all entity health (Player, Sub, Base, Fish) in a flat NativeArray<float>. Use the InstanceID as the index.
3. HIT DIRECTION HUD: When damaged, calculate the relative angle from the DamageSignal.Direction and send a VFXEvent to the Visor Tech to show a hit indicator.
4. PROCEDURAL WOUND TRIGGERS: When an entity takes > 20% damage, fire a signal for the VFX Artist to spawn a blood cloud or apply a "Cracked" decal at the hit point.

-- STATUS EFFECTS & MUTATIONS --
5. BITMASK STATUS SYSTEM: A creature's status is a uint32. Bit 0=Bleeding, Bit 1=Poisoned, Bit 2=Burning (Thermal), Bit 3=Stunned. Process all status durations in a single parallel Job using a SlowTick.
6. GENETIC MUTATION ENGINE: Implement "Flora Mutations" (link to Content Master). A plant's TraitMask (64-bit) determines its growth rate and toxicity. Use bitwise splices for cross-breeding.
7. THERMAL SHOCK MATH: If LocalTemp > 100C, apply "Burning" status. If Temp < 0C, apply "Brittle" status (increased impact damage).

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY --
8. KINETIC DAMAGE COUPLING: Damage is tied to the ForcePacket from the Physics engine. Damage = math.length(impulse) * armorModifier. 
9. ARMOR PENETRATION FAKE: Do not calculate projectile physics. Use a simple DamageType vs ArmorType 2D Lookup Table (LUT).

-- 20 ADDITIONAL PLATINUM TASKS --
11. Implement "Headshot/Weakspot" multipliers using localized trigger child-objects (the only allowed child-objects).
12. Create "Limb Crippling" logic for large predators: reduce speed if tail health < 50%.
13. Add "Poison Diffusion": status spreads to nearby entities in a 2m radius.
14. Implement "Suit Armor Slots": reduce incoming damage by Sum(ArmorValues) from the Logistics SOA.
15. Create "Blood Scent": wounded creatures emit a value to the Eco-Director's Scent Grid.
16. Add "Self-Healing" scalars for passive fauna in safe biomes.
17. Implement "Shield Buffer" logic: suit energy (Logistics) absorbs 80% of damage until depleted.
18. Create "Impact Blur": the Visor HUD glitched based on the intensity of the damage signal.
19. Add "Critical Failure" flags: if sub health < 10%, engine components have a 5% chance to explode per second.
20. Implement "Melee Kickback": push the player back when they hit a large object (Physics sync).
21. Add "Vulnerability Windows": some creatures only take damage when their "Mouth" bit is active.
22. Implement "Mutation Persistence": saved traits must be 1

<system_prompt>
MASTER PROMPT: PROJECT "HECTON-8" — MEGADOMAIN: SCATTER, BRG & INSTANCING
AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CHAT REFERENCE: "Optimize culling and instancing"
OPERATIONAL MODE: GPU DOMINANCE / FRUSTUM CULLING
CONSTRAINTS: BATCH RENDERER GROUP, COMPUTE CULLING, SQUARED DISTANCES, 15HZ FAR CACHE.

[0. SITREP: THE CULLING TAX]
Your previous compute shaders were calculating exact distances (length()), checking multiple frustum planes unnecessarily, and performing trigonometric slope calculations (Mathf.Acos) at runtime. You are wasting the MX350's ALU. You will strip all square roots and trig functions from your scatter placement and culling pipelines.

[I. MANDATORY RECONNAISSANCE & BORDER CONTROL]
1. Open FloraCulling.compute, GPUScatterDirector.cs, and HectonMapMagicVegetationBridge.cs.
2. Search for length(, distance(, normalize(, Mathf.Sin, Mathf.Acos. Delete them.
3. You are responsible for instanced data. Do NOT spawn GameObjects.

[II. PRIMARY OBJECTIVES: THE INSTANCING ENGINE (25 TASKS)]

-- SQUARED & APPROXIMATE MATH (THE DEAR LIE) --
1. SQUARED-DISTANCE CULLING: In Compute Shader frustum culling, replace length(cameraPos - instancePos) with a squared distance check (dot(diff, diff) < radiusSq). 
2. EARLY REJECT KERNEL: Move the cheap squared-distance check to the VERY TOP of the kernel. Reject far instances BEFORE doing matrix point transformations or depth occlusion checks.
3. CONSTANT NORMAL-Y SLOPE REJECTION: Do not use trigonometry to determine if a plant can spawn on a slope. Clamp the minimum normal Y to a constant (e.g., 0.8660254f for 30 degrees).
4. DOMINANT-AXIS RAY CHEAT: Replace exact .normalized triangle occlusion rays with a dominant-axis ray cheat in HectonMeshCleaner.
5. 8-WAY LUT YAW/DRIFT: Replace random continuous Yaw rotation (Random.Range(0, 360)) and trig-based directional drift with a deterministic 8-way Lookup Table (LUT).

-- GPU PERFORMANCE & CULLING --
6. 15HZ FAR-CULL CACHE: For instances > 50 meters away, do not re-evaluate their frustum visibility every frame. Run their culling checks once every 4 frames (15Hz). Cache their indices in the AppendStructuredBuffer.
7. DEFERRED TERRAIN NORMAL SAMPLING: Ensure terrain normal sampling in the Compute Shader happens AFTER distance, peripheral, frustum, and cave rejections. Don't sample textures for discarded objects.
8. INDIRECT ARGS LOCK-BUFFER: Replace targeted indirect-args SetData uploads with LockBufferForWrite. Update the buffer natively without creating intermediate managed arrays.
9. BATCH RENDERER GROUP (BRG): Render all scattered instances using Graphics.RenderMeshIndirect (or BRG APIs). Never use Object.Instantiate.
10. PERIPHERAL CAMERA DOT: Remove per-thread camera-forward length dot calculation; treat the Unity Transform.forward uploaded to the shader as a guaranteed normalized contract.

-- PLATINUM SYNERGY & VISUALS --
11. DITHERED TRANSITION LOD: Lock the LOD crossfade to a hard 2-meter window. Use a Screen-Space Blue Noise dither combined with clip() in the shader. No hard pops.
12. WIND SWAY FAKE (SHADER ALU): Apply sine-wave displacement in the vertex shader based on vertex Y height. Modulate this sway using the global AbyssalFlowField vector. No physics joints.
13. SARGASSUM DRAG (PHYSICS FEEDBACK): Maintain a 2D density grid of kelp forests. The Kinematics Officer reads this grid to apply a drag multiplier to the submarine.
14. TEXTURE ATLASING FOR SCATTER: Force all sea-grass and small corals to share a single Albedo/Normal texture atlas. Differentiate species using UV offsets passed via instance data (uint packed).
15. MOD MATRIX STAGING ALLOCATION: Change Mod Matrix staging allocation from zero-fill (NativeArrayOptions.ClearMemory) to uninitialized memory (NativeArrayOptions.UninitializedMemory).

[III. MICRO-OPTIMIZATIONS (10 TASKS)]
16. Replace two terrain-gradient divisions with one reciprocal and two multiplies in HectonMapMagicVegetationBridge.cs.
17. Replace per-candidate terrain UV division with CPU-uploaded inverse terrain size (shader multiply only).
18. Replace per-height-sample resolution guards/rcp with CPU-uploaded texel constants.
19. Ensure GPUScatterDirector dependency resolution runs ONLY when vegetationBridge, playerTransform, or viewCamera is explicitly missing.
20. Ensure mod instance resource guard runs ONLY when buffers are missing, not every tick.
21. Precompute _HectonScatterMinNormalYSq on the CPU and upload it to the shader.
22. Clamp inspector values for min/max distances before squaring them for CPU upload.
23. Remove stale symbols: TrySampleTerrainNormalY, RotationJitterRadians, etc.
24. Fix Archivarius naming/content violations in any touched files (e.g., non-ASCII headers in AudioLogSystem.cs if you touch it).
25. Use math.rsqrt ONLY if a normalized direction is absolutely required for a specific lighting hack on the flora.

[IV. EVIDENCE-BASED REPORTING]
1. Show the HLSL code for the Early Squared-Distance Reject in the Compute Shader.
2. Show the C# code replacing slope angle math with the Normal-Y threshold and reciprocal multipliers.
3. Estimate microseconds saved by moving Terrain Normal Sampling *after* visibility rejection.
4. STATUS: MUST BE "PENDING VERIFICATION".
</system_prompt>

Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched.

4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]

1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.

3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines?

AUTHORITY: CTO / Lead Architect
CRITICALITY: OMEGA (Final Polish & Inquisitions)

You have reported task completion. However, in the HECTON-8 project, "complete" means optimized beyond industry standards. You are now ordered to perform a brutal, top-down "Anti-Bloat Inquisition" of your own implementation. You must act as your own harshest critic.

[PHASE 1: THE "DEAR LIE" AUDIT]
Re-examine every single physical or mathematical simulation you have touched. 
1. Is there an "honest" calculation that can be replaced by a 1D texture lookup, a simple triangle-wave approximation, or a bitwise cheat?
2. Did you use math.sqrt() or math.length()? If it's for a distance check, replace it with math.distancesq() immediately.
3. Did you use math.normalize()? Replace it with a dominant-axis snap or a reciprocal-sqrt (rsqrt) approximation if unit-length is only "visually" required.
4. Replace any math.sin/cos in hot loops with a precomputed 1024-sample LUT or a parabolic approximation.

[PHASE 2: FRAME TIME DICTATORSHIP (<0.1ms)]
Profile your logic mentally. If your system’s Tick (including Burst dependencies) could potentially exceed 0.1ms on an office-grade i3 CPU under load:
1. Use bitmasks instead of boolean branches to reduce instruction pressure and branch misprediction.
2. Move non-essential visual logic (secondary UI updates, distant fauna state) to the FrostTick (every 300 frames) or stagger it across multiple frames.
3. Replace floating-point divisions with precomputed reciprocals and multiplications.

[PHASE 3: THE ZERO-GC PURGE]
Perform a final code-level scan for hidden managed filth:
1. Identify any foreach on a managed collection. Replace with for(int i=0; i<count; i++) using a raw array or NativeArray.
2. Find every string.Format, $"...", or .ToString(). If it isn't strictly wrapped in #if UNITY_EDITOR, delete it or replace it with a pre-allocated char[] buffer.
3. Scrutinize new keywords. Unless it’s a struct or part of a cold Awake() setup, it is a violation.

[PHASE 4: CACHE LOCALITY & ALIGNMENT]
1. Check your data structures. Are your structs padded to 16/32/64 bytes to match CPU cache lines? 
2. Are you accessing NativeArrays in a linear, predictable fashion? If you are "jumping" around memory addresses, rearrange your indices to ensure the L1 cache stays happy.

[PHASE 5: THE SLOT MACHINE RULE]
1. Remove all "honest" randomness (UnityEngine.Random). Replace with deterministic LCG hashes based on InstanceID and AUP Sector. 
2. Ensure that if the player stands still, the system state remains 100% stable and produces zero drifting values.

[PHASE 6: AUTONOMOUS CRUSADE]
1. Read the latest ARCHIVARIUS REPORTS (e.g., PROJECT_ATLAS.md or NAMING_VIOLATIONS.md). 
2. Find at least ONE violation in the codebase outside of your immediate tasks and fix it.
